<tr>
<td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;">
<div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
<ul>
<li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Socialism_sidebar" title="Template:Socialism sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Socialism_sidebar" title="Template talk:Socialism sidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Socialism_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>
</ul>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <b>Socialist International</b> (<b>SI</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Political_international" title="Political international">worldwide association of political parties</a>, most of which seek to establish <a href="/wiki/Democratic_socialism" title="Democratic socialism">democratic socialism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-statutes_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-statutes-1">[1]</a></sup> It consists mostly of democratic socialist, <a href="/wiki/Social_democracy" title="Social democracy">social-democratic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Labour_movement" title="Labour movement">labour</a> political parties and other organisations.</p>
<p>Although formed in 1951 as a successor to the <a href="/wiki/Labour_and_Socialist_International" title="Labour and Socialist International">Labour and Socialist International</a>, it has antecedents to the late nineteenth century. Initially dominated by parties from <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> it has grown to include 153 member parties<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> from over 100 countries. Its members have governed in many countries including most of Europe. The <a href="/wiki/Party_of_European_Socialists" title="Party of European Socialists">Party of European Socialists</a> (PES), a major <a href="/wiki/European_political_party" title="European political party">European political party</a>, is an associated organisation of the SI.</p>
<p>The current secretary general of the SI is <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Luis_Ayala_(politician)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Luis Ayala (politician) (page does not exist)">Luis Ayala</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> (<a class="extiw" href="https://www.wikidata.org/wiki/Q1517993#sitelinks-wikipedia" title="d:Q1517993"><span title='"Luis Ayala (politician)" in other languages'>other languages</span></a>)</span> (Chile), who has held the post since 1989.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-presidium_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-presidium-4">[4]</a></sup> The current president of the SI is the former <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Greece" title="Prime Minister of Greece">Prime Minister of Greece</a> <a href="/wiki/George_Papandreou" title="George Papandreou">George Papandreou</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-presidium_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-presidium-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Socialist_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WillyBrandtBerntCarlssonPenttiV%C3%A4%C3%A4n%C3%A4nen.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2485" data-file-width="3546" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/WillyBrandtBerntCarlssonPenttiV%C3%A4%C3%A4n%C3%A4nen.jpg/220px-WillyBrandtBerntCarlssonPenttiV%C3%A4%C3%A4n%C3%A4nen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/WillyBrandtBerntCarlssonPenttiV%C3%A4%C3%A4n%C3%A4nen.jpg/330px-WillyBrandtBerntCarlssonPenttiV%C3%A4%C3%A4n%C3%A4nen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/WillyBrandtBerntCarlssonPenttiV%C3%A4%C3%A4n%C3%A4nen.jpg/440px-WillyBrandtBerntCarlssonPenttiV%C3%A4%C3%A4n%C3%A4nen.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WillyBrandtBerntCarlssonPenttiV%C3%A4%C3%A4n%C3%A4nen.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Willy Brandt with outgoing secretary general <a href="/wiki/Bernt_Carlsson" title="Bernt Carlsson">Bernt Carlsson</a> (left) and new secretary general Pentti Väänänen (right) at the Socialist International Congress in 1983</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/International_Workingmen%27s_Association" title="International Workingmen's Association">International Workingmen's Association</a> (the First International) was the first international body to bring together organisations representing the <a href="/wiki/Working_class" title="Working class">working class</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELambDocherty2006176_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELambDocherty2006176-5">[5]</a></sup> It was formed in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> on 28 September 1864 by socialist, communist and anarchist political groups and trade unions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELambDocherty2006xxiv_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELambDocherty2006xxiv-6">[6]</a></sup> Tensions between moderates and revolutionaries led to its dissolution in 1876 in <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELambDocherty2006xxv_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELambDocherty2006xxv-7">[7]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Second_International" title="Second International">Second International</a> was formed in Paris on 14 July 1889 as an association of the socialist parties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELambDocherty2006302_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELambDocherty2006302-8">[8]</a></sup> Differences over <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> led to the Second International being dissolved in 1916.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/International_Socialist_Commission" title="International Socialist Commission">International Socialist Commission</a> (ISC, also known as Berne International) was formed in February 1919 at a meeting in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Berne" title="Berne">Berne</a> by parties that wanted to resurrect the Second International.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELambDocherty200652_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELambDocherty200652-9">[9]</a></sup> In March 1919 communist parties formed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comintern" title="Comintern">Comintern</a> (the Third International) at a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Founding_Congress_of_the_Comintern" title="Founding Congress of the Comintern">meeting in Moscow</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELambDocherty200677_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELambDocherty200677-10">[10]</a></sup> Parties which did not want to be a part of the resurrected Second International (ISC) or Comintern formed the <a href="/wiki/International_Working_Union_of_Socialist_Parties" title="International Working Union of Socialist Parties">International Working Union of Socialist Parties</a> (IWUSP, also known as Vienna International/Vienna Union/Two-and-a-Half International) on 27 February 1921 at a conference in <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELambDocherty2006177_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELambDocherty2006177-11">[11]</a></sup> The ISC and the IWUSP joined to form the <a href="/wiki/Labour_and_Socialist_International" title="Labour and Socialist International">Labour and Socialist International</a> (LSI) in May 1923 at a meeting in <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELambDocherty2006197_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELambDocherty2006197-12">[12]</a></sup> The rise of <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazism</a> and the start of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> led to the dissolution of the LSI in 1940. The Socialist International was formed in <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt" title="Frankfurt">Frankfurt</a> in July 1951 as a successor to the LSI.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELambDocherty2006320_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELambDocherty2006320-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the post-<a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> period, the SI aided social democratic parties in re-establishing themselves when dictatorship gave way to democracy in <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Revolution" title="Carnation Revolution">Portugal (1974)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_transition_to_democracy" title="Spanish transition to democracy">Spain (1975)</a>. Until its 1976 Geneva Congress, the SI had few members outside Europe and no formal involvement with <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> In the 1980s, most SI parties gave their backing to the <a href="/wiki/Sandinista_National_Liberation_Front" title="Sandinista National Liberation Front">Nicaraguan Sandinistas</a> (FSLN), whose <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Left-wing" title="Left-wing">left-wing</a> government had incited enmity from the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.</p>
<p>In the late 1970s and in the 1980s the SI had extensive contacts and discussion with the two leading powers of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> period, the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, on issues concerning East–West relations and arms control. The SI supported <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9tente" title="Détente">détente</a> and disarmament agreements, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SALT" title="SALT">SALT</a>II, <a href="/wiki/START_I" title="START I">START</a> and <a href="/wiki/Intermediate-Range_Nuclear_Forces_Treaty" title="Intermediate-Range Nuclear Forces Treaty">INF</a>. They had several meetings and discussion in <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a> with <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Carter" title="Jimmy Carter">Jimmy Carter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_United_States" title="Vice President of the United States">Vice-President</a> <a href="/wiki/George_H._W._Bush" title="George H. W. Bush">George Bush</a> and in <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a> with <a href="/wiki/General_Secretary_of_the_Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="General Secretary of the Communist Party of the Soviet Union">Secretaries General</a> <a href="/wiki/Leonid_Brezhnev" title="Leonid Brezhnev">Leonid Brezhnev</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev" title="Mikhail Gorbachev">Mikhail Gorbachev</a>. The SI's delegations to these discussions were led by the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Finland" title="Prime Minister of Finland">Finnish Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Kalevi_Sorsa" title="Kalevi Sorsa">Kalevi Sorsa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since then, the SI has admitted as member parties not only the FSLN but also the left-wing <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_Independence_Party" title="Puerto Rican Independence Party">Puerto Rican Independence Party</a>, as well as former <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">Communist</a> parties such as the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_of_the_Left" title="Democratic Party of the Left">Democratic Party of the Left</a> of Italy and the <a href="/wiki/FRELIMO" title="FRELIMO">Front for the Liberation of Mozambique</a> (FRELIMO).</p>
<p>Following the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tunisian_revolution" title="Tunisian revolution">Tunisian revolution</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constitutional_Democratic_Rally" title="Constitutional Democratic Rally">Constitutional Democratic Rally</a> was expelled from the SI in January 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SI170111_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-SI170111-16">[16]</a></sup> Later that month, the <a href="/wiki/National_Democratic_Party_(Egypt)" title="National Democratic Party (Egypt)">Egyptian National Democratic Party</a> was also expelled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SI310111_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-SI310111-17">[17]</a></sup> As a result of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%932011_Ivorian_crisis" title="2010–2011 Ivorian crisis">2010–2011 Ivorian crisis</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ivorian_Popular_Front" title="Ivorian Popular Front">Ivorian Popular Front</a> was expelled in March 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SI190311_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-SI190311-18">[18]</a></sup> However, according to section 5.1.3 of the statutes of the Socialist International, an expulsion requires a decision of Congress by a majority of two-thirds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 22 May 2013, the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" title="Social Democratic Party of Germany">Social Democratic Party of Germany</a> (SPD) along with other current and former member parties of the SI founded a rival international network of social-democratic parties known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Progressive_Alliance_(political_international)" title="Progressive Alliance (political international)">Progressive Alliance</a>, out of criticism of the perceived corrupt, undemocratic and outmoded nature of the SI.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Presidents.2C_honorary_presidents_and_secretaries_general">Presidents, honorary presidents and secretaries general</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Socialist_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Presidents, honorary presidents and secretaries general">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<div class="column">
<ul>
<li>XI <span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom"><img alt="United Kingdom" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Eastbourne" title="Eastbourne">Eastbourne</a> 1969</li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Consultative_parties">Consultative parties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Socialist_International&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Consultative parties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The following parties are consultative parties:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-members_25-3"><a href="#cite_note-members-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-broadleft_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-broadleft-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable sortable" style="text-align:left; font-size:95%">
<tr>
<th style="background:#d82628; color:#fff;">Country</th>
<th style="background:#d82628; color:#fff;">Name</th>
<th style="background:#d82628; color:#fff;">Abbr</th>
<th style="background:#d82628; color:#fff;">Government</th>
<th style="background:#d82628; color:#fff;">Notes</th>
